                                                           Central Avenue Traffic Memorandum




Executive Summary

The study corridor within the scope of this project consists of Central Avenue from 8 th
Street to Goodlette Frank Road in the City of Naples, Florida. The purpose of the study
is to provide traffic analysis in support of potential improvements along Central
Avenue, as part of the city’s redevelopment plan.

Central Avenue is currently classified as a four-lane section, however, the portion of
Central Avenue included in this project consists of several typical sections.

   ·   8th Street to 9th Street / US 41 – 2 Lane Roadway (1 EB / 1 WB) with exclusive
       eastbound and westbound left turn lanes.
   ·   9th Street / US 41 and 10th Street – 3 Lane Roadway (1 EB / 2 WB) with exclusive
       eastbound and westbound left turn lanes.
   ·   10th Street to 12th Street – 4 Lane Roadway (2 EB / 2 WB), no exclusive turn lanes
   ·   12th Street to Goodlette Frank Road – 3 Lane Roadway (1 EB / 2 WB), exclusive
       eastbound left turn lane.

Existing data were collected at two locations and supplemented by data from the City’s
count station along Central Avenue. Turning movement data were also collected at the
five intersections within the study area (8th Street, 9th Street / US 41, 10th Street, 12th
Street and Goodlette Frank Road).

Based upon discussion with the City of Naples, an identified improvement within the
study area includes the connection of 3 rd Avenue South to Goodlette Frank Road, which
will provide cross connectivity from US 41 to Goodlete Frank Road.

The Proposed Alternative consists of the following modifications:


   ·   Dedicated bicycle lanes in both east and west directions.
   ·   Raised medians.
   ·   On-street parking
   ·   Exclusive turn lanes along Central Avenue, where appropriate and conducive to
       traffic operations and safety.
   ·   Single lane roundabouts at 8th Street and 10th Street
   ·   Addition of a second eastbound left turn lane and an exclusive northbound right
       turn lane at Goodlette Frank Road.

Traffic analyses were performed, using seasonally adjusted data, for both opening year
(2016) and future year (2035) scenarios for both the No-build Alternative and the
Proposed Alternative. Future growth and traffic projections were based on data
obtained from multiple sources, including historical FDOT data, the Lee-Collier Travel
Demand Model and count data along Central Avenue (as provided by the City of Naples


                                                                                               i
                                                           Central Avenue Traffic Memorandum



count program). Under the Proposed Alternative, the study corridor is anticipated to
operate at an acceptable level of service and with available capacity in future year
conditions.

The signalized intersections (at 9th Street / US 41 and Goodlette Frank Road), analyzed
using seasonally adjusted data and inclusive of identified future developments within
the area, are anticipated to operate at acceptable levels of service. In addition, traffic
queues at 9th Street / US 41 are not generally anticipated to extend through the
roundabouts at 8th Street and 10th Street during the AM and PM Peak hours.

1     Introduction

This Traffic Technical Memorandum has been prepared by Kimley-Horn and
Associates, Inc. (KHA) on behalf of the City of Naples. The study corridor within the
scope of this project consists of Central Avenue from 8 th Street to Goodlette Frank Road
in the City of Naples, Florida. The project location is shown in Figure 1.

The purpose of the study is to provide a traffic analysis in support of potential
improvements along Central Avenue, as part of the city’s redevelopment plan. The
traffic memorandum includes the evaluation and documentation of existing conditions
and the roadway characteristics, as well as the development of design traffic volumes
for short-term (2016) and long-term (2035) future scenarios.


1.1   Description of Project

Central Avenue, an east-west local collector roadway, begins at the beaches to the
west and terminates just east of Goodlette Frank Road into the future Baker Park area.
Central Avenue is one of several east-west roadways which provide connection
between the two major north-south arterials in the area, US 41 and Goodlette Frank
Road, which are both 6-lane major arterials.

To the west of 8th Street, Central Avenue is a two-lane roadway with raised medians
and bicycle lanes. The portion of Central Avenue within the scope of this project is an
undivided roadway, with varying typical sections, no bicycle lanes, limited right-of-way
and several existing driveways which contribute to traffic operations and safety issues.
Figure 1 shows the project location.


1.2   Objective

The objective of this Technical Memorandum is to provide the City of Naples with the
analyses used to determine short term and long term traffic projections along Central
Avenue in support of the proposed improvements. Annual Average Daily Traffic
(AADT), Peak Hour Volume (PHV), intersection, and roadway Level of Service (LOS) are
detailed for existing conditions. In addition, this report includes the development of
future traffic forecasts and Level of Service analyses for the No Build and Build
Alternatives. Intersection operations analysis and anticipated turning movement queue
lengths are also documented.




                                                                                    Page 1
                                                        Central Avenue Traffic Memorandum



1.3   Methodology

The methodology for this report includes steps to collect existing data from multiple
sources, reviewing the adopted travel demand model for validity, develop existing year
design traffic volumes, and provide an operational analysis for existing roadways and
intersections. In addition, this report includes steps to review future land use data,
travel demand modeling, and projected growth to determine the anticipated future
year traffic volumes and future year operational analyses for existing roadways and
intersections.

2      Project Information

2.1    Project Location and Limits

Central Avenue, with the scope of this project is a local collector between 8 th Street and
Goodlette Frank Road, and is located within the City of Naples’ Community
Redevelopment Area. It provides access into the future Baker Park development, and is
one of several east-west roadways to provide cross connection between 9 th Street / US
41 and Goodlette Frank Road.


2.2    Existing Transit Service

Collier Area Transit (CAT) runs several routes along US 41 and Goodlette Frank Road in
the area, however, there are no fixed transit service routes along the study corridor of
Central Avenue. Figure 2 shows the existing transit services in the vicinity of the study
area.

                           Figure 2: Existing Transit Services*




       *Source: Collier Area Transit



                                                                                      Page 4
                                                           Central Avenue Traffic Memorandum




3       Existing Conditions

An analysis of existing operating conditions was conducted for the study area
segments and intersections. Data collection was conducted to establish existing
geometry, intersection turning movement counts, and segment counts. The results of
this data collection are presented in the subsequent tables and figures.


3.1     Existing Geometry

The existing geometry in the study area was obtained through review of aerial imagery,
and confirmed through field observations, and is shown in Figure 3. Central Avenue is
currently classified as a four-lane section, however, the portion of Central Avenue
included in this project consists of several typical sections.

    ·   8th Street to 9th Street / US 41 – 2 Lane Roadway (1 EB / 1 WB) with exclusive
        eastbound and westbound left turn lanes.
    ·   9th Street / US 41 and 10th Street – 3 Lane Roadway (1 EB / 2 WB) with exclusive
        eastbound and westbound left turn lanes.
    ·   10th Street to 12th Street – 4 Lane Roadway (2 EB / 2 WB), no exclusive turn lanes
    ·   12th Street to Goodlette Frank Road – 3 Lane Roadway (1 EB / 2 WB), exclusive
        eastbound left turn lane.

Central Avenue ends just east of Goodlette Frank Road. To the west, Central Avenue is
a two-lane divided roadway with raised medians (west of 6 th Street) and bicycle lanes
extending to the beach areas.

3.2     Traffic Count Information

Traffic counts were conducted in September 2014. Raw counts were adjusted by a
seasonal factor based on information from FDOT’s 2014 Florida Traffic Information
(FTI) publication. Intersection turning movement counts were conducted for each of the
following study intersections:

    ·   Central Avenue   &   8th Street
    ·   Central Avenue   &   9th Street / US 41
    ·   Central Avenue   &   10th Street
    ·   Central Avenue   &   12th Street
    ·   Central Avenue   &   Goodlette Frank Road

The counts were conducted during the AM Peak (7:00 AM to 9:00 AM) and PM Peak
(4:00 PM to 6:00 PM) periods. Segment counts were also conducted within the study
area. 72-Hour Volume Counts were conducted at the following locations:


                                                                                      Page 5
                                                         Central Avenue Traffic Memorandum



   ·   Central Avenue between 8th Street and US 41
   ·   Central Avenue between 12th Street and Goodlette Frank Road

Turning movement and segment count locations are shown in Figure 4.

The adjusted turning movement volumes for the AM and PM Peak Hours are shown in
Figure 5 and are detailed in Appendix A. Data from FTI is also included in Appendix
A.

In addition, quarterly counts published by the City were also used to supplement the
segment analysis. This count station is located on Central Avenue between 9 th Street /
US 41 and 10th Street. Traffic count summaries are provided in Appendix B.

3.3    Year 2014 Intersection Level of Service Analysis

Level of Service (LOS) is a qualitative measure used to describe the operational
conditions of an intersection, and is based on both delay and volume-to-capacity
ratios. The following table shows the delay ranges per LOS grade, per the Highway
Capacity Manual.

                               Table 1: Level of Service Thresholds

                                    LOS        Control Delay (sec / veh)
                                      A                     ≤ 10
                                      B                  > 10 - 20
                                      C                  > 20 – 35
                                      D                  > 35 – 55
                                      E                  > 55 – 80
                                      F                     > 80

Intersection analyses were conducted using Synchro (v8) Software. Existing signal
timings were provided by the City. Table 2 provides a summary of existing intersection
performance under AM and PM conditions.

                          Table 2: 2014 Existing Intersection Analysis

                                                             Intersection    Max V/C
          Study Intersection           Traffic Control                                      LOS
                                                             Delay (sec.)     Ratio
      AM PEAK HOUR
      Central Avenue @

        9th St. / US 41                    Signalized            32.8          0.80          C
        10th St.                           Signalized            7.8           0.30          A
        12th St.                          Unsignalized           1.9           0.16          B*
        Goodlette Frank Rd.                Signalized            13.1          0.58          B
      PM PEAK HOUR
      Central Avenue @
        8th St.                            Signalized            17.1          0.53          B

4     Development of Design Characteristics

Design Characteristics were developed using both the Project Traffic Forecasting (PTF)
Handbook and engineering judgement. The primary traffic design characteristics are
the Standard K factor and Design Hour Directional Demand (D). These characteristics
will be used in developing the future traffic volumes and conducting future operational
analysis.

4.1   Standard K Factor

The K Factor defines the proportion of daily volume that occurs within the peak hour.
FDOT has adopted a Standard K Factor to use in analysis based on area and facility
type. For arterials and highway within an urbanized area, the recommended K Factor is
9.0%. Therefore, a K factor of 9.0% will be used for the study area roadways.

4.2   D Factor
The Peak Hour Directional Demand (D) Factor is used to determine the directional split
of traffic during the design hour. Table 5 contains a summary of the measured D for
study area roadways, based on the 72-hour volume counts that were conducted in May
2013. As shown in the table, the average measured D for Central Avenue is 64.16%,
based on the counts conducted. Historical D values for US 41 and Goodlette Frank
Road were obtained from FDOT’s FTI publication.

                             Table 5: 2014 Measured D Factors

                         ROADWAY SEGMENT                           2013 Measured D Factor
          Central Ave
            8th St. to 9th St. / US 41                                    67.32%
            9th St. / US 41 & 10th St.                                    58.54%
            10th St. to 12th St.                                          64.66%*
            12th St. to Goodlette Frank Rd                                66.10%
                                                        Average:          64.16%
          US 41
            North of Central Ave                                          55.70%
          Goodlette Frank Road
            North of Central Ave                                          56.00%
             *Based upon data from adjacent segments.



The average field measured D value of 64.16% was used for Central Avenue, while a D
value of 56.00% was used for US 41, Goodlette Frank Road and the side streets.



                                                                                             Page 12
                                                           Central Avenue Traffic Memorandum




5       Development of Future Traffic Forecasts

Future traffic forecast volumes were developed for study area roadway segments.
Factors considered in the development of future traffic volumes include historic trends,
adopted future travel demand model volumes, population forecasts, and an
understanding of planned and programmed improvements.


5.1     Design Period

The following analysis years were used to evaluate conditions along the corridor:


    ·   Opening Year        –      2016
    ·   Future Year         –      2035


5.2     Programmed and Planned Improvements

A review was conducted of FDOT’s Five Year Work Program (2015-2019) and the
Collier County Metropolitan Planning Organizations (CMPO) Transportation
Improvement Program (2015-2019) to determine the planned and programmed
improvements in the study area. No capacity projects are currently programmed or
planned within the study area based upon this review.

Through discussion with City staff, an identified improvement within the vicinity of the
project includes the extension of 3 rd Avenue South to Goodlette Frank Road (3rd Avenue
South currently terminates at 12 th St). This extension would provide east-west
connectivity between US 41 and Goodlette Frank Road (in addition to Central Avenue
and 1st Avenue South), and provide additional access to these major arterials for local
traffic and direct access to the future Naples Square development.


5.3     Future Roadway Analysis Alternatives

The No Build scenario assumes no changes to the roadway in future conditions. The
Build traffic forecasts were developed assuming that Central Avenue, between 8 th Street
and Goodlette Frank Road, will be modified from a four-lane undivided roadway to a
two-lane divided roadway. In addition, the existing signalized intersections at 8 th Street
and 10th Street will be replaced by unsignalized roundabouts.




                                                                                     Page 13
                                                                      Central Avenue Traffic Memorandum



5.4    Future Travel Demand

In order to evaluate future conditions on the study area roadways, existing traffic data
must be projected to future analysis years. Historical growth and model growth were
evaluated and compared to determine the most appropriate method for projecting
future traffic volumes, based on the available information within the study area.

In order to determine an appropriate growth rate to apply to future traffic along
Central Avenue, several data sources were evaluated utilizing data from FDOT, Lee
County / Collier County MPO and the City of Naples.

5.4.1 FDOT Historical Growth

Available FDOT count data was obtained for three count stations near the vicinity of
the project corridor. Historical AADT data were obtained for the most recent ten year
span to determine a growth trend in the area.

Historical AADT data for all three count sites are summarized in Table 6 below, and
are included in Appendix D.

                             Table 6: FDOT Historical Growth Rates

Based on this review, historical growth is shown to be either trending downward or flat
over the most recent ten year span.

5.4.2 Lee / Collier Travel Demand Model Growth

The Lee / Collier Travel Demand Model was reviewed to determine the expected
growth rate between the 2007 base model and the 2035 long term model.
Socioeconomic data from Traffic Analysis Zones (TAZs) located within the City of
Naples’ CRA district were considered in the analysis. Table 7 below highlights the
expected growth based upon two separate variables: Total Population and Total
Employment.

                                                                                                       Page 14
                                                             Central Avenue Traffic Memorandum



    Table 7: Travel Demand Model Population and Employment Growth in the CRA

                                               TOT_POP TOT_EMP
                         2007 Total Volume      2,595        9,544
                         2035 Total Volume      4,039       13,678
                               Total Change     1,444       4,134
                                % Change        55.6%       43.3%
                          Annual % Change       2.0%         1.5%

As indicated, and assuming trip making characteristics will remain similar to existing
conditions, the overall growth in population within the City of Naples Community
Redevelopment Area is approximately 2%, while the growth in employment is
approximately 1.5%. TAZ data is shown in Appendix E.

5.4.3 City of Naples Historical Growth

A review of historical growth along Central Avenue was performed utilizing traffic
count data (count station located between 9th Street / US 41 and 10th Street) from the
City of Naples. Table 8 below shows the Historical Annual Growth recorded over the
most recent 10 year period.

                   Table 8: Central Avenue Historical Growth Rates

                        Year            Mar.    June       Sept.     Dec.
                        2014           8,697    5,197      5,070     7,320
                        2013           7,359    4,799      4,771     6,041
                        2012           7,040    4,849      4,683     5,454
                        2011           6,990    4,855      4,331     6,858
                        2010           6,717    5,000      4,284     5,977
                        2009           6,903    4,935      4,328     5,501
                        2008           7,049    5,087      4,652     5,600
                        2007           8,656    3,463      3,035     6,776
                        2006           8,606    6,420      5,788     6,152
                        2005           9,003    6,029      3,497     6,912

                   Annual Growth      -0.38%   -1.64%   4.21%        0.64%

                     Average
                                                   0.71%
                   Annual Growth

This review shows an average annual growth rate of less than 1% as measured by the
City’s count data.




                                                                                       Page 15
                                                             Central Avenue Traffic Memorandum



5.4.4 Conclusion

The review of growth highlights several key trends along Central Avenue and within the
immediate study area. Although the review of the demand model yielded an overall
growth rate of 2%, this represents the anticipated growth (based upon socio-economic
data) within the entire CRA area, taking into account that the downtown area is primed
for redevelopment. This growth also represents analysis zones that are outside of the
immediate vicinity of the study corridor (but still within the CRA) that may use US 41
and Goodlette Frank Road.

Comparatively, historic traffic along US 41, Goodlette Frank Road and 5 th Avenue South
shows a downward trend over the last ten years. Central Avenue, a local roadway,
serves local east-west travel, while US 41 and Goodlette Frank Road (6-lane major
arterials) primarily provides connectivity between the north and south parts of Collier
County. To account for these roadway characteristics the growth rates to be used in
the Future Conditions analyses are as follows:


   ·   2% annual growth along US 41 and Goodlette Frank Road
   ·   1% annual growth along Central Avenue
   ·   1% annual growth along 8th Street, 10th Street and 12th Street


5.5    Future AADT Volumes

Future AADT volumes were developed by applying the annual growth rate to the actual
roadway volumes along Central Avenue. This growth rate was applied to the existing
AADT along Central Avenue as shown in the table below.

volumes were calculated and are shown in Table 9.

5.6   Intersection Design Hour Volumes

Future year intersection design hour volumes (DHV) were developed using the future
year AADT projections, in combination with the design characteristics, and the turning
movement counts collected at the study intersections. Raw volumes were seasonally
adjusted and grown to 2035 future year volumes. In addition, traffic from previously
identified developments/redevelopments, as provided by the City, were also included
for both AM and PM peak hour analyses.

The AM and PM design hour volumes for both Opening Year (2016) and Future Year
(2035) are included in Figure 6 and Figure 7. Turning movement development
worksheets are located in Appendix F.

6       Future Conditions Analysis

An analysis of future conditions was conducted for No Build and Build conditions for
Opening Year and Future Year scenarios.


6.1     Geometry – Proposed Alternative

The Proposed Alternative roadway geometry assumes that Central Avenue will be
modified from a four-lane undivided roadway to a two-lane divided roadway. Limits of
the widening are from 8th Street to the east of Goodlette Frank Road. Associated
intersection improvements include:


    ·   Dedicated bicycle lanes in both east and west directions.
    ·   Raised medians.
    ·   On-street parking.
    ·   Exclusive turn lanes along Central Avenue, where appropriate and conducive to
        traffic operations and safety.
    ·   Single lane roundabouts at 8th Street and 10th Street
    ·   Addition of a second eastbound left turn lane and an exclusive northbound right
        turn lane at Goodlette Frank Road.

Figure 8 shows the build conditions of the proposed roadway configuration. The
future Proposed Alternative corridor plan is shown in Appendix G.

7       Summary and Conclusions

This Design Traffic Technical Memorandum (DTTM) has been prepared to provide
design traffic volumes and traffic analysis for the Central Avenue Improvements
project.


8.3     Proposed Alternative

The Proposed Alternative roadway geometry assumes that Central Avenue will be
widened modified from a four-lane undivided roadway to a two-lane divided roadway
in the future conditions. Limits of the widening are from west of 8 th Street to the
Goodlette Frank Road. Associated intersection improvements include:


    ·   Dedicated bicycle lanes in both east and west directions.
    ·   Raised medians.
    ·   On-street parking.
    ·   Exclusive turn lanes along Central Avenue, where appropriate and conducive to
        traffic operations and safety.
    ·   Single lane roundabouts at 8th Street and 10th Street
    ·   Addition of a second eastbound left turn lane and an exclusive northbound right
        turn lane at Goodlette Frank Road.

All study area roadway segments under the Proposed Alternative scenario are
anticipated to operate at an acceptable LOS under Opening Year (2016), and Future
Year (2035) conditions.

Based on the intersection analyses, all study area intersections are anticipated to
operate acceptably under Opening Year (2016) and Future Year (2035) conditions.

Anticipated queue lengths at the signalized intersections are not generally expected to
extend through the roundabouts at 8th Street and 10th Street, under Opening Year
(2016) and Future Year (2035) conditions.
